Chapter 1

ãŸã‚ã«ãªã‚‹ï¼è€ƒãˆã•ã›ã‚‰ã‚Œã‚‹è©±


How Rich Are We?

è‡ªåˆ†ãŸã¡ã¯ã©ã‚Œãã‚‰ã„è±Šã‹ãªã‚“ã ã‚ã†ï¼Ÿ

çœŸã®è±Šã‹ã•


ã‚ã‚‹æ—¥ã€ãŠé‡‘æŒã¡ã®çˆ¶è¦ªãŒã€å®¶æ—ã‚’ç”°èˆã®è¾²å ´ã§ã®ä¸€æ³ŠäºŒæ—¥ã®æ—…ã«é€£ã‚Œã¦è¡Œã£ãŸã€‚å®Ÿã¯çˆ¶è¦ªã«ã¯ã²ãã‹ã«ã€ä¸–ã®ä¸­ã«ã¯è²§ã—ã„äººã‚‚ã„ã‚‹ã“ã¨ã‚’æ¯å­ã«æ•™ãˆãŸã„ã¨ã„ã†æ„å›³ãŒã‚ã£ãŸã®ã ã€‚æ—…ã®å¾Œã€çˆ¶è¦ªãŒæ¯å­ã«æ„Ÿæƒ³ã‚’èã„ã¦ã¿ã‚‹ã¨......ã€‚



DL01_How Rich Are We?

ã€€One day, a rich father took his family on a trip into the*1country, with the*2firm intention of showing his son just how poor some people were. They spent a day and a night on the farm of a very poor family. They worked hard with them, ate with them, and in the evening relaxed with them, before falling*3fast asleep,*4exhausted from their hard day's work. The next morning they thanked the poor family and*5waved goodbye as they drove back to their*6luxurious home in the city.

ã€€When they finally sat down at home, the father asked his son, "How was the trip?" "Really good, Dad! Everyone was so happy and friendly." "Ah, yes, but did you see how poor they were?" the father asked. "Yeah, I guess." "So, what did you learn?" The son answered, "I saw that we have a pool that reaches to the middle of the garden; they have a river that has no end. We have imported lamps in the garden; they have the stars. Our*7patio reaches to the front yard; they have a whole*8horizon. And I learned that if there was a problem, everyone joined in to*9get it fixed."

ã€€When the little boy was finished, his father didn't know what to say. His son added, "Thanks, Dad, for showing me how 'poor' we are!"

226words


The point of this story

Imagine a poor person. Nearly everyone will think of a person lacking money or food. Few, if any, will think of a happy person. However, as the boy in this story*10highlights, having a greater number of things does not necessarily mean having greater happiness.

DL02_The Pencil Story

ã€€The pencil maker*1took a new pencil aside, just before putting him into the box. "There are five things you need to know," he told the pencil, "before I send you out into the world. Always remember them, and you will become the best pencil you can be."

ã€€"One: you will be able to do many great things, but*2only if you think of the*3whole picture."

ã€€"Two:*4from time to time your*5point will become*6blunt and you will not be able to*7perform as well as you'd like to, but don't let this problem*8stop you from trying."

ã€€"Three: you will make mistakes."

ã€€"Four: the most important part of you will always be what's inside."

ã€€"And five: in every place you are used, you must leave your*9mark. No matter what your condition, you must continue to write."

ã€€The pencil understood and promised to remember, and went into the box with*10purpose in its heart.


ã€€Now put yourself*11in the pencil's place. Always remember these things and you will become the best person you can be.

ã€€One: you will be able to do many great things, but only if you think of the whole picture. It's very easy to forget the important things in life by*12concentrating on your own little world. You must always remember to work*13for the good of everyone and not just for the good of yourself.

ã€€Two: from time to time you may feel there is no point in your life, when everything you try fails, but*14disappointments should make you*15value the things you have and help you better understand the problems of others.

ã€€Three: you will make mistakes --- everybody does. The important thing is to do your best to learn from them,*16so as not to repeat those mistakes in the future.

ã€€Four: the most important part of you will always be what's on the inside. If you look beautiful on the outside, that may get you noticed, but unless you are beautiful on the inside, people will not return to you and you will lead a lonely life.

ã€€And, five: in every place you go, you must leave your mark. No matter what the situation, you must continue to do your*17duty.


ã€€Allow this story of the pencil to*18encourage you. Yes, life can be painful and we all make mistakes, but you can live a satisfying and useful life if you think of others as well as yourself.

409words


The point of this story

It is easy to believe that life is*19complicated, but there are a few simple things we should not forget. Just like a pencil, we have the ability to be*20productive, but we must also remember to*21think of the bigger picture.

DL03_From Here to Here

ã€€An American businessman was by the sea in a little Mexican village when a small boat with just one fisherman arrived. Inside the small boat were several large fish. The American told the Mexican how good the fish looked and asked how long it had taken to catch them. The Mexican replied that it had only taken a short*1while.

ã€€The American then asked why he didn't stay out longer and catch more fish. The Mexican said that he had caught enough for himself and his family.

ã€€The American then asked, "But what do you do with the rest of your time?" The fisherman said, "I*2sleep late, fish a little, play with my children, take a*3siesta with my wife, Maria, and*4wander into the village each evening, where I drink wine and play guitar with my friends. I have a*5full and busy life, sir."

ã€€The American laughed. "I'm a Harvard*6MBA and I could help you," he said. "You should spend more time fishing and with the extra money you make, buy a bigger boat. With the extra money earned fishing from the bigger boat, you could buy several boats and one day you could have 10, 15, maybe 20 fishing boats! Instead of selling your*7catch at the local market, you could sell directly to the fish factories. But why stop there? You could open your own*8cannery. You would control the product,*9processing and*10distribution. You would need to leave this little village and move to Mexico City, then probably LA and onto New York City, where you could*11run your great fishing business."


ã€€The fisherman asked, "But sir, how long will all this take?"

ã€€The American replied, "Fifteen years."

ã€€"But then what, sir?"

ã€€The American laughed and said, "That's the best part. When the time is right, you would sell your company*12stock to the public and become very rich. You would make millions!"

ã€€"Millions, sir? Then what?"

The point of this story

This story*13encourages us to think about our goals in life. Many people jump into a career without considering what they really hope to*14achieve. The goal of earning more and more is not a*15worthwhile goal in itself. It is easy to*16overlook the pleasure that the simple things in life can bring.

DL04_Put the Glass Down

ã€€A teacher was talking to her students about stress management. She raised a glass of water and asked them, "How heavy do you think this glass of water is?"

ã€€The students' answers*1ranged from 20 to 500 grams.

ã€€"*2As a matter of fact, how heavy it is doesn't depend on how much the water actually*3weighs. It depends on how long you hold it."


ã€€"If I hold it for a minute, it's OK. If I hold it for an hour, my arm will start to hurt. If I hold it for a day, you may have to call an*4ambulance! It is the exact same weight, but the longer I hold it, the heavier it becomes."

ã€€"*5The same goes for our*6burdens. If we carry them around with us all the time they will start to*7weigh us down.*8Sooner or later we will not be able to*9carry on."

ã€€"What you have to do is to put the glass down and rest for a while, before lifting it up again."


ã€€We have to put down our burdens from time to time, so that we can get our energy back and carry on. So be sure to make time for yourself each day to put all of your cares and troubles aside and just relax.


ã€€You can always pick them up later. Whatever burdens are weighing you down, forget about them for a moment if you can.


ã€€Pick them up again when you've rested. Life is short; enjoy it!

249words


The point of this story

A well-known proverb summarizes this story perfectly: "*10All work and no play makes Jack a dull boy." If we don't put down our burdens from time to time, we, and our lives, will become dull. To*11revitalize ourselves and our lives, we need to rest, to take time off and to relax.

DL05_Keep Your Fork

ã€€There was a young*1religious woman who had been told she was dying and*2had been given three months to live. So as she was getting her things "*3in order," she contacted her*4priest and asked him to come to her house to discuss certain details of her*5final wishes.

ã€€She told him which songs she wanted to be sung at her*6funeral service, what Bible stories she would like to be read out, and what clothes she wanted to be*7buried in.


ã€€Everything was almost in order, and the priest was preparing to leave when the young woman made her final and most important request.

ã€€"There's one more thing," she said calmly.

ã€€"What's that?" came the priest's reply.

ã€€"This is very important," the young woman continued. "I want to be buried with a fork in my right hand."

ã€€The priest stood looking at the young woman, not knowing quite what to say.

ã€€"I suppose that surprises you, doesn't it," the young woman said.

ã€€"Well, to be honest, I am*8puzzled by the request," said the priest.

ã€€The young woman explained. "My grandmother once told me a story, and from that time I have always believed in its message. I have also always tried to*9pass that message on to those I love and those who are finding life hard."


ã€€"My grandmother told me this: 'In all my years of attending*10socials and dinners, I always remember that when the dishes of the main course were being*11cleared, someone would*12lean over and say, "Keep your fork." It was my favorite part, because I knew that something better was coming --- like*13velvety chocolate cake or*14deep-dish apple pie. Something wonderful, and worth waiting for!' "

ã€€"So, I just want people to see me lying there in that*15coffin with a fork in my hand, and I want them to wonder, 'What's with the fork?' Then I want you to tell them: 'Keep your fork ... The best is*16yet to come.' "

ã€€The priest's eyes filled with tears as he said goodbye to the young woman. He knew this would be one of the last times he would see her before her death. But he also knew that the young woman had a stronger*17belief in heaven than he did. She had a stronger belief in what heaven would be like than many people twice her age with twice as much experience and knowledge. She truly believed that something better was coming.


ã€€At the funeral, people were walking by the young woman's coffin and they saw the clothes she had chosen and the fork in her right hand.*18Over and over, the priest heard the question: "What's with the fork?" And over and over he smiled.

ã€€During his*19message, the priest told the people of the conversation he had had with the young woman before she died. He also told them about the fork and about what it meant to her. The priest told the people how he could not stop thinking about the fork and told them that they probably would not be able to stop thinking about it either.

ã€€So the next time you reach down for your fork, let it remind you,*20ever so gently, that the best may be yet to come.

543words


The point of this story

Everyone has worries and disappointments at times. There are times in life when things*21get us down, when all the good times can seem to be in the past. This story reminds us not to give up hope, because often the future may hold even better times.

The Present

DL06_The Present

ã€€Imagine there was a bank that each morning*1credited your account with*2a large sum of money. But, it carried over no*3balance from day to day. Every evening it removed whatever part of the balance you failed to use during the day. What would you do? Draw it all out, of course!

ã€€Each of us does have such a bank. Its name is Time. Every morning, it credits you with 86,400 seconds. Every night it*4writes off as*5lost whatever of this you have failed to use*6to good purpose. It*7carries over no balance. It allows no*8overdraft. Each day it gives you 86,400 shiny new seconds to use*9as you please. Each night it burns the*10remains of the day. If you fail to use the seconds, minutes and hours of the day, the loss is yours. There is no going back. There is no*11drawing against tomorrow. You must live in the*12present on today's hours.*13Invest them wisely so as to get the best in health, happiness, and success!

ã€€The clock is running.*14Make the most of today. And remember that time waits for no one. As*15Eleanor Roosevelt wrote, "Yesterday is history. Tomorrow is mystery. Today is a gift. That's why it's called the present."

211words


The point of this story

Time is*16precious. Everyone has wasted time in the past, but the good thing is that as you read this you have more time. So don't waste it! Right now, you can start*17afresh and use your time exactly as you choose.

DL07_Memos from Your Child

ã€€Don't be too upset if I say, "I hate you." I don't really hate you; I'm just sad because you don't understand me.

ã€€Don't*1correct me in front of people if you can*2help it. I'll*3take much more notice if you talk to me*4in private.

ã€€Don't complain all the time. If you do, I shall soon stop listening.

ã€€Don't*5question my*6truthfulness too much. I am easily frightened into telling lies.

ã€€Don't tell me my fears are silly. They are terribly real to me, and you can help me understand them.


ã€€Don't*7spoil me. I know I can't have everything I ask for ... I'm only testing you.

ã€€Don't be afraid to*8be firm with me. I prefer it ... it*9teaches me right from wrong.

ã€€Don't make me feel that my mistakes are crimes. You should judge me on my*10intentions, not my*11failures.

ã€€Don't try to protect me from everything. Sometimes I need to learn*12the hard way.

ã€€Don't forget I love*13experimenting. It's the best way for me to learn, so please put up with it.


ã€€Don't make promises you can't keep. It will make me lose trust in you.

ã€€Don't say no one day, but yes the next. That completely puzzles me and makes me*14lose faith in you.

ã€€Don't*15put me off when I ask you questions. If you do, you'll find that I stop asking you and start looking elsewhere for advice.

ã€€Don't ever suggest that you are perfect. It will give me*16too great a shock when I discover that you're not.

ã€€Don't forget that I cannot explain myself as well as I would like. That is why I'm not always*17accurate.


ã€€Don't think you should never say sorry to me. Saying sorry shows me I am important, and brings me closer to you.

ã€€Don't forget how quickly I am growing up. I know it must be very difficult for you to keep pace with me, but please try.

ã€€Don't forget that I can't grow without lots of love. The more I receive, the more I'll be able to give.


ã€€And please keep yourself*18fit and healthy. I need you.

357words


The point of this story

Many children hear adults telling them, "Don't do this," and "Don't do that." It's worth remembering that if the roles were*19reversed our children would also like to tell us not to do a great number of things. So, just as we expect them to do everything we say, we must consider whether our own behavior reaches the high standards we*20demand of our children.

Installing Love

æ„›ã‚’ã‚¤ãƒ³ã‚¹ãƒˆãƒ¼ãƒ«

è‡ªå·±ã¨ä»–è€…ã¸ã®æ„›

DL08_Installing Love

Tech Support: Yes ... how can I help you?

Customer: Well, my system doesn't seem to be running*1properly, so after much thought, I decided to*2install Love. Can you guide me through the*3installation process?

Tech Support: Yes. I can. Are you ready to start?


Customer: Well, I'm not very technical, but I think I'm ready. What do I do first?

Tech Support: The first step is to open your heart. Have you found your heart?

Customer: Yes, but there are several other programs running now. Is it OK to add Love while they are still running?

Tech Support: What programs are they?

Customer: Let's see, I have past-*4hurt.*5exe, low-*6self-esteem.exe,*7jealousy.exe and*8dislike.exe running right now.

Tech Support: No problem, Love will*9gradually*10remove past-hurt.exe from your*11operating system. It may remain in your*12permanent memory but it will no longer*13affect other programs. Love will gradually*14replace low-self-esteem.exe with a program of its own called high-self-esteem.exe. However, you have to*15completely*16turn off jealousy.exe and dislike.exe. Those programs*17prevent Love from being properly set up on your system. Can you turn those off?


Customer: I don't know how to turn them off. Can you tell me how?

Tech Support: With pleasure. Go to your start menu and open*18never-mind.exe. Do this as many times as necessary until jealousy.exe and dislike.exe have been completely removed.

Customer: OK, done! Love has started opening. Is that normal?

Tech Support: Yes, but remember that you only have the base program. You need to begin connecting to other hearts in order to get it working properly.

Customer: Oops! I have an error message already. It says, "Error --- program cannot run on other systems." What should I do?

Tech Support: Don't worry. It means that the Love program is not set up to run on your heart yet. In non-technical terms, it simply means you have to love yourself before you can love others.


Customer: So, what should I do?

Tech Support:*19Pull down self.exe; then*20highlight the following files: forgive-self.*21txt; realize-your-worth.txt; and know-your-limits.txt.

Customer: OK, done.

Tech Support: Now, copy them to the "My Heart" folder. The system will*22overwrite any files that were stopping your heart from running smoothly. Also, you need to remove*23self-hatred.txt from all folders and then restart your system to make sure it is completely gone and never comes back.

Customer: Got it. Hey! My heart is filling up with new files. I can already see that smile.*24mpg has started working, and peace.txt and happiness.txt are copying themselves all over my heart. Is this normal?


Tech Support: Sometimes. For others it takes a while. So, it sounds like Love is running correctly. One more thing before we*25hang up. Love is*26freeware. Be sure to share it with everyone you meet. They will share it with others*27in turn and return some*28cool stuff back to you.

Customer: I will. Thank you for your help.

487words


The point of this story

If we open our hearts we will find love. Holding on to negative feelings from the past will not make us happy. Wave goodbye to the bad feelings about others. The point of this story is that when you show love and kindness toward others --- and yourself --- then love and kindness will come back to you.

DL09_Mother's Day

ã€€A man stopped at a flower shop to order some flowers to be sent to his mother, who lived 200 miles away. He knew it would be better if he could actually go and see his mother, but these days he just*1didn't seem to have any free time.*2Besides, he was sure she would understand.

ã€€As he got out of his car, he noticed a young girl sitting by the bus stop crying. "Hey,*3what's up?" he asked. "*4Missed your bus?" "Oh no, the bus doesn't matter; I can walk," she replied. "But I wanted to buy a red rose for my mother. The trouble is I only have 75 cents, and a rose costs two dollars." The man smiled and said, "Come on in with me. I'll buy you a rose."

ã€€He bought the little girl her rose and ordered his own mother's flowers. As they were leaving he offered the girl a*5ride home. "That would be great," she said. "If you're sure you don't mind, you can take me to my mother." "No problem. Just tell me which way," he answered.

ã€€After a few minutes driving the girl asked the man to stop, and he*6pulled up to*7let her out. The girl thanked the man and said goodbye.*8It wasn't until she was walking*9hurriedly through the gates that he realized she was entering a*10graveyard.*11Instead of*12driving off, the man*13watched on*14in disbelief as the girl*15bent down and placed the rose on a*16freshly dug grave.


ã€€Wiping the tears from his eyes, the man knew*17at once what he should do. Life is too short to spend worrying about work and deadlines and all of those other little duties that*18eat up your free time. We have to make time for the truly important things. He drove straight back to the flower shop, canceled his order, and bought a big*19bunch of flowers. He then drove the 200 miles to his mother's house.

332words


The point of this story

As we*20go about our daily*21routines, spring turns to summer, and autumn to winter. Time passes so quickly that it's easy to overlook the people we love --- the people we think of as always there. This story reminds us that we can never tell them we love them too often.

What Is Love?

æ„›


ã€Œæ„›ã¨ã¯ï¼Ÿã€------ ã‚ã‚‹å¿ƒç†å­¦è€…ãŒå‡ºã—ãŸå“²å­¦çš„ãªå•ã„ã«4æ­³ã‹ã‚‰8æ­³ã®å­ã©ã‚‚ãŸã¡ãŒç­”ãˆã¦ã„ã‚‹ã€‚å­ã©ã‚‚ãŸã¡ã®è¨€è‘‰ã¯ã€æ·±ãæ¸©ã‹ã„ã‚‚ã®ã°ã‹ã‚Šã€‚ãƒ”ãƒ¥ã‚¢ãªãƒãƒ¼ãƒˆã‹ã‚‰ã¤ã‚€ãå‡ºã•ã‚ŒãŸã€Œæ„›ã€ã®å½¢ã¨ã¯ï¼Ÿ



DL10_What Is Love?

ã€€Some*1psychologists asked a group of 4- to 8-year-olds the following question: "What is love?" The answers they got were broader and deeper than anyone could have imagined. See what you think:


ã€€"When my grandmother got old, she couldn't*2bend over and paint her*3toenails anymore. So now my grandfather does it for her --- even though his hands hurt a lot these days. That's love." Rebecca --- aged 8

ã€€"When someone loves you, the way they say your name is different. You just know that your name is safe in their mouth." Billy --- aged 4

ã€€"Love is when you give somebody most of your*4French fries without making them give you any of theirs." Chrissy --- aged 6

ã€€"Love is what makes you smile when you're tired." Terri --- aged 4

ã€€"Love is when my mommy makes coffee for my daddy and she drinks a little bit before giving it to him, to make sure the taste is OK." Danny --- aged 7

ã€€"Love is what's in the room with you at Christmas, if you stop opening presents and listen." Bobby --- aged 7

ã€€"Love is when you tell a guy you like his shirt, then he wears it every day." Noelle --- aged 7

ã€€"Love is like a little old woman and a little old man who are still happy to see each other, even though they've lived together for their whole lives." Tommy --- aged 6

ã€€"During my school*5play, I was on stage and I was very*6nervous. I looked at all the people watching me and saw my daddy waving and smiling. He was the only one doing that. I wasn't nervous anymore." Cindy --- aged 8

ã€€"My mommy loves me more than anybody. I know because she always kisses me to sleep at night." Clare --- aged 6

ã€€"Love is when Mommy gives Daddy the best piece of chicken." Elaine --- aged 5

ã€€"Love is when Mommy sees Daddy*7smelly and*8sweaty and still says he is more handsome than Brad Pitt." Chris --- aged 7

ã€€"Love is when my pet dog*9licks my face when I come home after leaving him*10on his own all day." Mary Ann --- aged 4

ã€€"I know my older sister loves me because she gives me all her old clothes and has to go out and buy new ones." Lauren --- aged 4

ã€€"When you love somebody, your*11eyelashes go up and down and little stars come out of you." Karen --- aged 7

ã€€"You really shouldn't say 'I love you' unless you*12mean it. But if you mean it, you should say it a lot. People forget." Jessica --- aged 8

429words


The point of this story

As the story shows, love is not just one thing. Love shows itself in many ways. If you think about all of those ways, you will*13realize that there is much more love in your life than maybe you thought.

Eleanor Roosevelt

ã‚¨ãƒ¬ãƒã‚¢ãƒ»ãƒ«ãƒ¼ã‚ºãƒ™ãƒ«ãƒˆã¯ã€20ä¸–ç´€ã«æ´»èºã—ãŸå¥³æ€§ã¨ã—ã¦ã€ã‚¢ãƒ¡ãƒªã‚«ã§æœ€ã‚‚å°Šæ•¬ã•ã‚Œã¦ã„ã‚‹å¥³æ€§ã®ä¸€äººã ã€‚ç¬¬32ä»£ã‚¢ãƒ¡ãƒªã‚«å¤§çµ±é ˜ãƒ•ãƒ©ãƒ³ã‚¯ãƒªãƒ³ãƒ»ãƒ«ãƒ¼ã‚ºãƒ™ãƒ«ãƒˆã®å¦»ã§ã‚ã‚Šã€å¥³æ€§ã‚„ãƒã‚¤ãƒãƒªãƒ†ã‚£ãƒ¼ã«é–¢ã™ã‚‹æ”¿ç­–ã§ã¯å¤«ã«å¤§ããªå½±éŸ¿ã‚’ä¸ãˆãŸã€‚æ™©å¹´ã€å¤«ã¨æ­»åˆ¥ã—ãŸå¾Œã¯ã€ä¸–ç•Œäººæ¨©å®£è¨€ã®èµ·è‰ã«ã‚‚è²¢çŒ®ã™ã‚‹ãªã©ã€ãƒªãƒ™ãƒ©ãƒ«æ´¾ã®é‹å‹•å®¶ã¨ã—ã¦ã‚‚æ´»èºã—ãŸã€‚å½¼å¥³ã¯ä¸€ä½“ã€ã©ã®ã‚ˆã†ãªç”Ÿæ¶¯ã‚’é€ã£ãŸã®ã ã‚ã†ã‹ï¼Ÿ



DL11_Eleanor Roosevelt

ã€€In America, Eleanor Roosevelt is*1seen as one of the most important women of the 20th century. Married to President Franklin Roosevelt, she became the First Lady of the United States in 1933. But she is remembered even more for helping the poor and improving*2civil rights at a time when many people believed that women could never do anything important.


ã€€Eleanor was the daughter of a wealthy*3public figure in New York, and her early life was luxurious. But she also had plenty of*4grief. Eleanor's mother often made her young daughter*5self-conscious by pointing out her*6plain looks, and sometimes*7playfully called her "*8granny" because of the way she acted old-fashioned for her age. But sadly, Eleanor was only 8 years old when her mother died. Her father also*9passed away less than two years later, and Eleanor was alone.

ã€€Forced to live with her grandmother, Eleanor found herself lonely. Her life was*10stable, but not very loving. Her grandmother's only concern was Eleanor's education. Eleanor was not allowed to play like normal children, and her grandmother expected her to speak only if she was spoken to first. As a result, she had trouble*11fitting in*12socially with other children her age.

ã€€When Eleanor was sent to*13boarding school in England, it*14gave her a welcome break from her lonely childhood. She became an*15eager, intelligent and popular student. And after three years at boarding school, she had truly*16come out of her shell.

ã€€When Eleanor returned to New York in 1902, her grandmother expected her to*17blend in with other*18high-society women. But Eleanor wasn't very excited about the fancy-dress parties she was expected to attend. The parties did, however, introduce her to some of the people that would later change her life.

ã€€Like many other young women in her social circle, Eleanor became part of the*19New York Junior League. The group was a women's social organization that did volunteer work and helped the poor. Along with a friend, Eleanor visited the poorer areas of New York in order to teach exercise lessons and dancing to young girls. Later she began to visit factories for the first time, and*20witnessed some of the terrible working conditions there. The work helped Eleanor to understand how protected and*21privileged her youth had been.


ã€€Fortunately, she was able to share these experiences with a new friend --- a distant cousin named Franklin Delano Roosevelt. She once asked him to*22accompany her during her social work so that he could see the*23poverty for himself. Franklin*24was deeply moved by what he had seen, and amazed at Eleanor's intelligence and kindness. Happily, Eleanor had found someone who matched her*25intellectually and emotionally. And on*26St. Patrick's Day in 1905, the couple was married.

ã€€Their relationship faced one of its toughest challenges when Franklin became*27paralyzed from the*28waist down*29due to a disease. He was forced to put aside his rising political career, and spent a long time trying to improve his health. Eleanor had to*30take over as the head of the family, looking after their five children while helping to*31nurse Franklin. While Franklin never fully recovered, he became well enough to return to active political life. With Eleanor behind him, He was elected*32governor of New York in 1929, and four years later became president of the United States.


ã€€Eleanor became one of Franklin's closest advisers in the White House, and they traveled around the country. Now used to*33public speaking, she even became the first "First Lady" to hold a*34press conference of her own, and in a surprising decision, invited only women reporters to attend.

ã€€But perhaps the proof of Eleanor's*35determination came when the*36Daughters of The American Revolution, a group she had been a member of, refused to let the African-American opera singer Marian Anderson perform in their building. Mrs. Roosevelt quit the organization to*37protest this*38racist decision, and gave her support to the free public concert that was later organized at the*39Lincoln Memorial.


ã€€Eleanor Roosevelt*40accomplished many more*41incredible things in her life. Despite her lonely, privileged background, Eleanor worked hard to learn about the lives of*42ordinary people, and then to help improve them. She once wrote, "You must do the thing you think you cannot do." And*43it is unlikely that anyone imagined that the young girl who had been teased for being plain and old-fashioned would grow up to become such a strong, modern woman. Eleanor Roosevelt gave many of America's most*44neglected people a happier future, because she believed in doing what she thought she could not do.

771words


The point of this story

Eleanor Roosevelt was born into privilege. However, so too were we. If you look at the world, you will see there are many people*45much worse off than you. Eleanor's story should be a*46reminder that there is a greater world beyond our own*47cozy, social circles. We can all find and help*48people in need.

What Is Happiness?

å¹¸ã›ã¨ã¯ï¼Ÿ

è¶³ã‚‹ã‚’çŸ¥ã‚‹å¿ƒ


èº«ãªã‚Šã‚‚é«ªå‹ã‚‚ãã¡ã‚“ã¨ã—ãŸã€92æ­³ã®ã™ã¦ããªãŠã°ã‚ã•ã‚“ãŒè€äººãƒ›ãƒ¼ãƒ ã«ç¾ã‚ŒãŸã€‚ä»Šæ—¥ã‹ã‚‰ãƒ›ãƒ¼ãƒ ã§ã®æš®ã‚‰ã—ã‚’ã‚¹ã‚¿ãƒ¼ãƒˆã™ã‚‹ã‚ˆã†ã ã€‚éƒ¨å±‹ã«æ¡ˆå†…ã•ã‚Œã‚‹é€”ä¸­ã«å®¤å†…ã®æ§˜å­ã‚’çœ‹è­·å¸«ã‹ã‚‰èã„ãŸãŠã°ã‚ã•ã‚“ã¯......ã€‚



DL12_What Is Happiness?

ã€€A*1petite and*2proud 92-year-old lady, who is fully dressed each morning by 8 o'clock in perfectly ironed clothes, with her hair fashionably done, even though she is almost blind, moved to our*3nursing home today. Her*4husband of 70 years recently passed away, making the*5move necessary.


ã€€After many hours of waiting for me quietly in the*6reception of the nursing home, she smiled*7brightly when I told her that her room was ready.

ã€€As she moved her*8walker to the elevator, I provided a*9visual description of her tiny room, including the curtains that had been hung on her window. "I love it," she*10stated, like an 8-year-old who had just been given a new toy.

ã€€"Mrs. Jones, you haven't seen the room yet."

ã€€"That*11doesn't have anything to do with it," she replied. "Happiness is something you decide on*12ahead of time. Whether I like my room or not doesn't*13depend on how the furniture is arranged, it's how I arrange my mind. I've already decided to love it."

ã€€"You have?"


ã€€"Sure. It's a decision I make every morning when I wake up. I*14have a choice: I can spend the day in bed worrying about the parts of my body that no longer work, or I can get out of bed and be happy about the ones that do. Each day is a gift, and as long as my eyes open, I'll welcome the new day and enjoy all the happy memories I've*15stored away just for this time in my life."

256words


The point of this story

It may sound surprising, but this story tells us that we can choose to be happy. If you think that you are not going to like something, you will be looking for bad things to confirm your*16prejudice. On the other hand, if you decide that you are going to like something, you will approach it positively --- looking for everything good about it. So, whether something makes you happy or not, largely depends on your*17attitude.

DL13_This Is Good

ã€€There was once an African king who had a very good friend. They had*1grown up together, and now that they were*2men they still spent every day*3in each other's company. The friend was always fun to be with because he had such a bright and happy attitude toward life. In fact, whatever happened, whether good or bad, the friend would always say, "This is good!"


ã€€One day the king and his friend were out hunting. The friend was*4loading and preparing the guns for the king.*5Unfortunately the friend did something wrong when preparing one of the guns, and after taking the gun from his friend, the king*6fired it and his*7thumb was*8blown off.*9Examining the situation, the friend said as usual, "This is good!" To which the king replied, "No, this is*10definitely not good!" and he sent his friend to*11jail.

ã€€About a year later, the king was hunting in an area that he should have known to*12stay clear of. As he*13crept quietly into a dark forest, he suddenly went from being a hunter to being the hunted. He was surrounded by*14cannibals, who caught him and took him back to their village. They*15forced him to lie on top of a large pile of wood, and then began*16tying his feet and hands to the wood. But just as they*17were about to set fire to the wood, one of them screamed, noticing that the king was missing a thumb. They believed that eating someone who was less than whole would bring them bad luck. So they released the king and*18sent him on his way.


ã€€As he returned home, the king remembered how he had lost his thumb and*19felt terrible for the way he had treated his friend. He*20immediately went to the jail to speak with his friend. "You were right," he said, "itwas good that my thumb was blown off." He told his friend about his lucky*21escape. "And so I'm very sorry for sending you to jail for so long. It was bad of me to do this."

ã€€"No," his friend said, "This is good!" Shocked, the king asked, "What do you mean, 'This is good'? How could it be good that I sent you to jail for a year?" His happy friend replied, "If I had not been in jail, I would have been with you."

402words


The point of this story

Just because something bad happens to us, it does not mean that nothing good will*22come of it. For example, such disappointments as, "If I had got into the best university ..." or, "If I hadn't missed the bus ..." or, "If I had not broken up with my partner ..." may all be followed by, "I would never have met you!"

DL14_Last Respects

ã€€One day not too long ago, the employees of a large company in Chicago, Illinois, returned from their lunch break and were*1greeted by a message. Some received the message by e-mail, others as a*2handwritten note, but they each received exactly the same message: "Yesterday, the person who has been stopping your growth in this company passed away. We invite you to come and*3pay your last respects in the gym."


ã€€At first everyone was sad to hear that someone in the company had died, but after a while they began to wonder who this person might be. They also thought it a little strange that they would be gathering in the gym for such a sad occasion. Wouldn't a church be better?

ã€€When the employees began arriving at the gym, they still had no idea who had died. They were all trying to think who it was who had been stopping their*4progress. And*5privately they*6were all relieved that the person would not be there to stop them any longer.

ã€€One by one the employees moved closer, until they reached the spot where the*7body had been laid out. At that point, they each in turn became silent as they looked down. They stood there shocked, as if someone had placed a cold hand on their shoulder.

ã€€What they saw when they looked down was a mirror: everyone who looked at it saw themselves. There was also a sign below the mirror that read: "There is only one person who can*8set limits to your growth: you."


ã€€When everyone had read the message, the*9CEO of the company arrived in the gym. All the employees knew that the company had been doing badly, but the CEO told them that if things didn't change soon, the company would have to close. It had been his idea for everyone to pay their last respects to their*10former selves. He explained that if everyone worked to their full*11potential, the company could*12become a success again. The workers left the gym motivated, and determined to do what they could to make their future and the future of their company a success.

361words


The point of this story

To achieve success, we should not set limited goals. We can all find reasons to explain why our lives are not better. For example, we can*13blame our luck, or our boss, or*14politicians ... Maybe*15there is some truth in these*16excuses but, as this story makes clear,*17beneath it all there is one common thing : you. If you set small goals, your*18achievements will be small.

The Cracked Pot

ã²ã³ã®å…¥ã£ãŸã‹ã‚

å€‹æ€§ã®å¤§åˆ‡ã•ã¨è‡ªå°Šå¿ƒ


ã‚¤ãƒ³ãƒ‰ã®ã‚ã‚‹æ°´é‹ã³äººã¯æ¯æ—¥ã€ä¸»äººã®åŸã¾ã§å¤§ããªäºŒã¤ã®ã‹ã‚ã§æ°´ã‚’é‹ã‚“ã§ã„ãŸã€‚å®Ÿã¯ã€ç‰‡æ–¹ã®ã‹ã‚ã«ã¯ã²ã³ãŒå…¥ã£ã¦ã„ã¦ã€ãã®ã‹ã‚ã¯ã€åŸã¾ã§æº€æ¯ã®æ°´ã‚’é‹ã¹ãªã„è‡ªåˆ†ã‚’ã„ã¤ã‚‚è²¬ã‚ã¦ã„ãŸã®ã ãŒ......ã€‚



DL15_The Cracked Pot

ã€€A water*1carrier in India had two large*2pots, each*3hung on the end of a pole which he carried across his shoulders. One of the pots was perfectly made with no*4cracks or holes. The other pot had a crack in it, so that by the time the water carrier reached his*5master's house it was only half full.

ã€€This situation went on daily for two years, with the carrier delivering only one and a half pots of water to his master's house. Of course, the perfect pot was proud that it was doing such a good job. But the*6poor cracked pot was*7ashamed of its*8fault, and disappointed that it was only able to manage half of what it was supposed to do.

ã€€After two years of this bitter failure, the cracked pot spoke to the water carrier one day by the*9stream. "I am ashamed of myself, and I want to say sorry to you." "Why?" asked the carrier. "What are you ashamed of?" "I have been able, for these past two years, to deliver only half my load, because this crack in my side lets the water*10drip out all the way back to your master's house. Because I'm not perfect, you have to do all of this work, without getting*11full value for your efforts," the pot said.

ã€€The water carrier was surprised that the old cracked pot felt this way, and said, "As we return to the master's house, I want you to notice the beautiful flowers along the path."


ã€€So, as they went up the hill, the old cracked pot*12took notice of the sun warming the beautiful wild flowers at the side of the path, and this cheered it a little. But at the end of the journey, it still felt bad for having let half of its water drip away, and so again the pot said sorry to the carrier for its failure.

ã€€The carrier said to the pot, "Didn't you notice that the flowers were only on your side of the path, and not on the other pot's side? That's because I have always known about the crack in your side, and I*13took advantage of it. I planted flower*14seeds on your side of the path, and every day while we walked back from the stream, you've*15watered them. For two years I have been able to enjoy watching these beautiful flowers grow. I've also picked them to display on my master's table. Without you*16being just the way you are, he would not have had this beauty to*17grace his house."


ã€€From that day forward, the cracked pot knew that what it had thought of as a weakness was actually a strength. Now on their daily journey along the path, the cracked pot was proud of the water dripping from the crack in its side.

478words


The point of this story

*18The fact of the matter is that we're all cracked pots. Each of us has our own unique faults. But if we accept them, we can use these differences to make the world a more interesting and better place.*19After all, if everyone was exactly the same, there would be no surprises, no discoveries to be made,*20indeed, no beauty in the world. So, don't be afraid of what you may think of as your faults. Accept them and remember that there is no such thing as*21perfection, and it is only through our differences that we can make a beautiful world together.

Determination and Persistence

DL16_Determination and Persistence

ã€€In the 1860s, a*1creative engineer named John Roebling had the surprising idea of building an*2enormous bridge across the East River connecting New York with Brooklyn. Nothing like it had ever been tried before, and many bridge-building experts*3claimed that it was an impossible task. They told Roebling to forget the idea. The*4engineering was too difficult, and the river was much too wide.


ã€€Roebling did not listen. He thought about the bridge all the time. He could see in his head how it had to be built, and he wanted to try. But first he needed help. Roebling began talking about the project with his son Washington. Washington was an*5up-and-coming engineer as well, and after some discussion he decided to join his father.

ã€€Working together, the father and son developed several new ways that such a long bridge could be made strong enough to carry so much weight.*6Full of excitement for the challenge ahead of them, the two Roeblings hired a*7crew. Then they began to*8measure the land and choose the*9exact place where the bridge would stand.

ã€€Unfortunately, early in the project, John Roebling was injured in an accident. At first, his injury seemed*10minor, but soon, it caused an*11infection which became worse and worse. The infection took John Roebling's life, but before he died, he*12put Washington in charge of the Brooklyn Bridge project.

ã€€Sadly, Washington's luck was not much better. Only three years after his father's death, Washington also became ill and, as a result, was forced to stay in bed. Unable to leave the house, Washington was only able to watch the bridge being built through a*13telescope at his window. And the project*14wasn't even close to being finished.

ã€€Washington's wife, Emily Roebling, became both his nurse and his assistant. Emily*15fought for her husband's*16right to continue as chief engineer for the bridge project. She helped to*17convince everyone that Washington was still able to do the engineering work that the bridge needed. With Washington's help, Emily studied engineering and mathematics until she too had become an expert. She traveled back and forth from the bridge, giving Washington's instructions to the workers, and returning to Washington with information about the bridge's progress.


ã€€For the next 11 years, Washington and Emily worked together to finish the Brooklyn Bridge. Emily spoke to workers, politicians and engineers, and*18earned the respect of many people. When the bridge was finally opened in 1883, Washington wasn't able to go to the opening ceremony. However, he watched with pride as his wife became the very first person to cross the bridge.

ã€€Today the beautiful Brooklyn Bridge*19stands as a symbol of patience and*20perseverance. It started only as John Roebling's dream. Yet, despite the accidents and*21setbacks, the bridge was finally built through hard work, the understanding and*22drive of a family, and the love that held them together even in difficult times.

ã€€Perhaps this is one of the best examples of a*23never-say-die attitude, an attitude that allowed Washington and Emily Roebling to succeed despite a series of terrible events. Together they built*24what was then the world's longest*25suspension bridge.


ã€€Often, when we face problems in our everyday life, they are much smaller than the problems that other people have to face. The Brooklyn Bridge is one example of a project that seemed impossible at first, but was finished because of the*26persistence and determination of people who worked hard and supported one another, no matter what the*27odds were.

588words


The point of this story

This story is obviously about how hard work and determination can succeed, despite the negative opinions of others. But there is more that we can take from this story. We should not*28be too ready to say something is impossible. Just because something has never been done before does not mean it will not be done in the future. Let's try to encourage*29ambitious people, not discourage them.

Growing Good Corn

ãŠã„ã—ã„ã¨ã†ã‚‚ã‚ã“ã—ã‚’è‚²ã¦ã‚‹ç§˜ã‘ã¤

ä»–è€…ã¸ã®è²¢çŒ®


å·ã®å“è©•ä¼šã«ã¨ã†ã‚‚ã‚ã“ã—ã‚’å‡ºå“ã—ã€ã»ã¼æ¯å¹´å„ªå‹ã—ã¦ã„ã‚‹è¾²å ´ä¸»ãŒã„ãŸã€‚ã‚ã‚‹æ–°èè¨˜è€…ãŒã€è³ªã®è‰¯ã„ã¨ã†ã‚‚ã‚ã“ã—ã‚’è‚²ã¦ã‚‹ç§˜ã‘ã¤ã‚’æœ¬äººã«å°‹ã­ã¦ã¿ã‚‹ã¨......ã€‚



DL17_Growing Good Corn

ã€€Once, there was a Nebraska farmer who grew excellent corn. Each year he entered his corn in the*1state fair, where it almost always won the*2blue ribbon prize.

ã€€One year a newspaper reporter interviewed the farmer and*3learned something interesting about how he grew his corn. The reporter discovered that the farmer shared his*4seed corn with his neighbors.


ã€€"*5How can you afford to share your best seed corn with your neighbors, when they are entering corn in the same competition as you each year?" the reporter asked.

ã€€"Aren't you worried that their corn will win instead?"

ã€€"Well, sir," said the farmer, "it's not only the seeds --- it's how you grow the corn. When it's windy, the*6pollen from the corn plant is picked up by the wind, and it flies out over all the nearby fields. If my neighbors grow corn that isn't as good as mine, their pollen will mix with my plants, and my*7quality will go down, too. If I want to grow good corn, I have to help my neighbors grow good corn."

ã€€The explanation made the reporter understand the*8connectedness of*9living things --- how the conditions in one field could*10touch all the fields around it.


ã€€He realized that this was not only true in farming. If you hope to live in happiness, you will be more successful if you also help your neighbors to live in happiness. If you don't,*11it won't be long before the unhappiness around you begins to affect you, too. After all, the value of one life is*12measured by the lives it touches.

266words


The point of this story

This story shows us the importance of sharing. If you know someone who is usually happy and friendly, it's likely that that person is also someone who is good at sharing. People who try to keep their good fortune to themselves often spend their time*13worryingly*14guarding what they have, and have less time to relax and make friends.

DL18_Thanks for Your Time

ã€€It had been some time since Jack had seen the old man. College,*1girls, career and life itself*2got in the way. Jack moved*3across the country following his dreams. He had*4launched an*5architectural design office the previous year, and in the*6rush of his busy life, he had little time to think about the past and often no time to spend with his wife and son. He was busy*7working on his future.


ã€€Over the phone, his mother told him, "Mr. Belser died last night. The funeral is Wednesday."

ã€€"It's been so long since I thought of him. I thought he must have died years ago," Jack said.

ã€€"Well, he didn't forget you," Mom told him. "Every time I saw him he'd asked how you were doing. He'd tell me about all the days you spent over 'his side of the fence'*8as he put it,"

ã€€Memories*9flashed through Jack's mind as he remembered his childhood days. "He's the one who taught me*10carpentry," he said. "I wouldn't be in this business*11if it weren't for him. He spent a lot of time teaching me things he thought were important ..."

ã€€"You know, Jack, after your father died, Mr. Belser*12stepped in to make sure you had a man's influence in your life," she said.

ã€€"Mom, I'll be there for the funeral," Jack said.

ã€€*13As busy as Jack was, he*14kept his word. Mr. Belser's funeral was small and*15uneventful. He had no children of his own, and most of his relatives had passed away.


ã€€The night before Jack had to return home, he and his Mom stopped by to see the old house next door one more time.

ã€€Stepping into the house, Jack felt like he was*16stepping back in time. The house was exactly as he remembered, and every step held memories. Every picture, every piece of furniture ... Jack stopped suddenly.

ã€€"What's wrong, Jack?" his Mom asked.

ã€€"The box is gone," he said.

ã€€"What box?" she asked.

ã€€"There was a small gold box that he kept locked on top of his desk. I must have asked him a thousand times what was inside. All he'd ever tell me was, 'The thing I*17value most,'" Jack said.

ã€€It was gone. Everything about the house was exactly how Jack remembered it, except for the box. He*18figured someone from the Belser family had taken it.

ã€€Two weeks later, returning home from work, Jack discovered a note in his mailbox. "Signature required on a package. Please stop by the main post office within the next three days," the note read.

ã€€The next day Jack*19collected the package. It was old and looked like it had been mailed a hundred years ago, but the*20return address*21caught his attention.

ã€€"Mr. Harold Belser," it read.

ã€€Jack took the package out to his car and opened it. There inside was the gold box and an envelope. Jack's hands shook as he read the note inside.

ã€€"Upon my death, please*22forward this to Jack Bennett. It's the thing I valued most in my life." A small key was taped to the letter. His heart*23racing, Jack opened the box. There inside he found a beautiful gold*24pocket watch.

ã€€He carefully*25unlatched its cover, on the inside of which were written these words: "Jack, Thanks for your time! --- Harold Belser."

ã€€"The thing he valued most was ... my time."


ã€€Jack held the watch for a few minutes, then called his office and cleared his appointments for the next two days. "Why?" his assistant, Janet, asked.

ã€€"I need to spend some time with my son," he said. "Oh, by the way, Janet ... thanks for your time!"

609words


The point of this story

There is a lot of loneliness in the world, and yet spending time with people is such a simple thing to do. We can see how*26grateful the old man was for the time Jack spent with him. This story encourages us to think about who we might be neglecting.

Subway Hero

åœ°ä¸‹é‰„ã®ãƒ’ãƒ¼ãƒ­ãƒ¼

ãƒ’ãƒ¼ãƒ­ãƒ¼


ãƒ‹ãƒ¥ãƒ¼ãƒ¨ãƒ¼ã‚¯ã®åœ°ä¸‹é‰„ã§é›»è»Šã‚’å¾…ã£ã¦ã„ãŸè‹¥ã„å¤§å­¦ç”ŸãŒã€ã‘ã„ã‚Œã‚“ã‚’èµ·ã“ã—ã¦ç·šè·¯ã«è»¢è½ã—ã¦ã—ã¾ã£ãŸã€‚è¿‘ãã«ã„ãŸç”·æ€§ã¯ã€å¤§å­¦ç”Ÿã‚’åŠ©ã‘ã‚‹ãŸã‚ã«ãŸã‚ã‚‰ã†ã“ã¨ãªãç·šè·¯ã«é£›ã³é™ã‚ŠãŸã€‚é›»è»Šã¯ã”ã†éŸ³ã‚’ã¨ã©ã‚ã‹ã›ãªãŒã‚‰ã€äºŒäººã«è¿«ã£ã¦ãã‚‹......ã€‚



DL19_Subway Hero

ã€€It was a normal January afternoon in New York for Wesley Autry. Wesley had just picked up his two daughters, aged 4 and 6, and was taking them home before heading to work himself.

ã€€As the three of them waited for the subway train to arrive, a young college student standing near the*1tracks suddenly began to shake, then he fell to the floor. Wesley and two other women tried to help the young man, but after a few moments the student seemed to*2recover.*3Shakily, he stood up, then suddenly fell over*4backward --- right onto the train tracks.

ã€€Knowing the train was coming soon, Wesley acted quickly. He asked one of the women to watch his daughters, and jumped down onto the tracks. Wesley had hoped to lift the student back onto the platform, but the man was*5confused and weak.

ã€€Then, Wesley felt the*6rush of air and he heard the sound of a train. Looking up, he saw the bright lights coming quickly toward them. He was out of time.

ã€€Wesley did the only thing he could do. Quickly, he pushed the student into the low space between the tracks, and then lay on top of him. Wesley held the student's arms and legs down so he could not move, and said, "Sir, please don't move! If you move, one of us is going to die!"

ã€€Unable to stop, the train ran right over top of the two men, its brakes making a terrible noise. People on the platform shut their eyes*7in horror. When the cars finally came to a stop, there was silence. Then, a voice came up from beneath the train: "We're OK down here!"

ã€€The crowd on the subway platform*8burst into*9cheers.

ã€€"I've got two daughters up there," continued Wesley. "Let them know their daddy's OK!"

ã€€In the days and weeks to come, Wesley*10was showered with praise.*11Donald Trump offered Wesley a check for $10,000; Wesley's family was given free rides for a year on the subway, and a one-week trip to Disney World; and the school that the young student had been attending offered to teach Wesley's daughters for free.

ã€€But on that day --- after dusting himself off and seeing the young man safely*12in the care of hospital staff --- Wesley simply*13headed off to work. He was happy to have done the right thing.

395words


The point of this story

This story is based on a true event. In 2007, Wesley Autry did really save a young man on the subway. It shows that we do not need money or special*14treatment to make us feel happy. The important thing is not how much praise or reward we get, but to simply do what we think is the right thing. That should be enough.

The Story of Kyle

ã‚«ã‚¤ãƒ«ã®è©±

å‹æƒ…ã¨æ€ã„ã‚„ã‚Š


ã‚ã‚‹ç”·å­é«˜æ ¡ç”ŸãŒä¸‹æ ¡ã®é€”ä¸­ã€è»¢æ ¡ç”Ÿã®ã‚«ã‚¤ãƒ«ãŒã„ã˜ã‚ã‚‰ã‚Œã¦ã„ã‚‹ã®ã‚’ç›®æ’ƒã—ãŸã€‚ãŸãŸãè½ã¨ã•ã‚ŒãŸæ•™ç§‘æ›¸ã‚„çœ¼é¡ã‚’æ‹¾ã†ã®ã‚’æ‰‹ä¼ã£ãŸãã®æ—¥ã‚’ãã£ã‹ã‘ã«ã€äºŒäººã¯è¦ªå‹ã¨ãªã‚‹ã€‚æœˆæ—¥ã¯ãŸã¡å’æ¥­å¼ã‚’è¿ãˆãŸãã®æ—¥ã‚ã‚‹çœŸå®ŸãŒæ˜ã‚‰ã‹ã«......ã€‚



DL20_The Story of Kyle

ã€€One Friday, when I was walking home from high school, I saw the new kid, Kyle. It looked like he was carrying all of his books. I*1thought to myself, "Why would anyone take home all their books on a Friday? He must be a real*2nerd." I went back to thinking about my own weekend plans: football with my friends, then later a party.

ã€€As I walked on, I saw*3a bunch of kids running toward Kyle. They*4ran into him, knocking the books out of his arms and*5tripping him so he*6landed*7in the dirt. His glasses went flying, and I saw them land in the grass about 10 feet away. He looked up so sadly, almost crying.

ã€€So I went over and helped him pick up his books, and handed him his glasses. "Those guys are so stupid," I told him. Kyle started to smile and said, "Hey thanks!" I could see I'd really cheered him up.*8As it turned out, Kyle had only moved to the area a few weeks earlier, but those guys had done the same thing to him nearly every day. "But they won't be doing it again!" he said angrily. "Forget them Kyle," I said, and invited him to play football on Saturday with me and my friends. He said yes.

ã€€It was a great weekend with Kyle and my friends, and the more we got to know him, the more we all liked him. Monday morning came, and there was Kyle with all his books again. "Sorry, you didn't get much time to look at all those books," I joked. He just laughed and handed me half of them to carry.

ã€€Kyle and I became best friends, and over the next four years although he never took all his books home on weekends, he did find plenty of time to study. Now that we were*9seniors, he was planning to be a doctor, while I was going to study for business on a football scholarship. A lot of things had changed during our time at high school, but especially for Kyle. Each year, one student is chosen by the teachers to make a speech at the high school leaving ceremony. This year they had chosen Kyle.

ã€€As he started his speech, he*10cleared his throat, and began, "This is a time of year for thanking all those who helped us*11make it through high school --- our parents, our teachers, our sisters and brothers, but mostly our friends. I am here to tell all of you that being a friend to someone is the best gift you can give them. I am going to tell you a story."


ã€€I could not believe my ears as Kyle began to tell everyone the story of the day we first met. He had been planning to*12kill himself that weekend! He talked of how he had taken all the books from his locker so his mom wouldn't have to do it later. Then, once more, those guys had attacked him. "But, I was saved. My friend saved me."

ã€€I heard the*13gasp go through the crowd as this*14ordinary, yet now popular, boy told us all about his weakest moment. "If you remember one thing that I say," Kyle continued, "remember that we all have the power to change people's lives. On that unhappy day, my friend could have kept walking but he chose to help me. And that changed everything. We all have the power to make other people happy or sad, not just for a minute but for a lifetime."

598words


The point of this story

Small acts of kindness can have great*15consequences. By simply being kind to others in our daily lives, we can make the world a better place.

DL21_Grameen Bank

ã€€In 1974, serious flooding in Bangladesh caused a terrible*1famine. Throughout Bangladesh, an*2estimated one million people*3starved to death over the next few years.

ã€€During the famine, a concerned young professor at Chittagong University, Muhammad Yunus, was*4upset that all he could do to help society was teach economics. He wanted to do more to help*5his fellow countrymen and women. He wanted to*6put away the economic theories and textbooks and find out about the real lives of the poor of Bangladesh. With this in mind, he took his students on a*7field trip to the local village of Jobra.

ã€€In Jobra, the professor and his students met a woman named Sophia who made small bamboo seats*8for a living. They were shocked to discover that she only made 2 cents a day from her work. Most of her money went into paying back*9high-interest loans that she used to buy the*10raw materials she needed. Their research in Jobra*11revealed many more poor people living just like Sophia.

ã€€*12Traditional banks would not lend money to these poor people because they did not trust the poor to pay them back. So, villagers such as Sophia had to borrow money from local dealers, who*13charged*14awfully high interest rates. None of the villagers could make enough money to escape their*15poverty because they were all having to pay back high-interest loans.

ã€€Yunus saw that if these people could borrow money at a more reasonable rate, it would help them greatly. So he*16lent 42 poor women the $27 he had with him to buy raw materials to make their bamboo seats, etc.*17Crucially he trusted these*18penniless women to pay him back --- if they didn't, there would be nothing he could do.

ã€€Yunus's lower*19repayment rate allowed the women to make enough to live on and to make a profit. He continued his banking system for the poor based*20purely on trust, and it soon became successful in several villages. So in 1983, Yunus decided to start his own bank, Grameen Bank, with the single purpose of loaning money to the "poorest of the poor." The word "gram" means village in*21Bengali, reflecting the bank's*22origins.

ã€€Grameen Bank has a unique system. To get a loan, all you need to show is that you are poor and you have the*23desire to work hard. Then, five of you make a group and each of you receives a small individual loan. People who borrow from the bank*24repay the trust they are given by repaying their loans*25in record numbers.


ã€€If one of the group cannot repay their loan, the rest of the group will*26suffer. This social pressure encourages the members to pay back on time. However, the rest of the group do not have to repay an unpaid loan --- Grameen Bank accepts it as a loss. By trusting these people with their tiny loans, Yunus allowed them to help themselves.

ã€€It is an interesting fact that about 97 percent of Grameen borrowers are women. Yunus believes that women living in poverty use the money more directly for their families than men. Not only do they repay their loans, but they also*27clothe, educate and feed their children with their profits.

ã€€Over the last few years, the*28greed and mistakes of traditional banks have caused great problems in the world economy. At the same time, Grameen Bank has continued to make life a little better for the poor of the world. The contrast between these banks and Grameen Bank is*29obvious: they work to make money; Grameen works to help the poor.


ã€€Grameen Bank has*30so far loaned about $6.4 billion to 7.4 million families, and now many financial*31institutions around the world have copied Muhammad Yunus's simple model. It is worth remembering that the poor are not poor because they are*32lazy. They are no different from the rich. They just happen to have been born into different families. In 2006, the great work done by Yunus and the bank itself was*33recognized, and they were*34awarded the*35Nobel Peace Prize.

683words


The point of this story

This story*36demonstrates the power of trust. Muhammad Yunus and his Grameen Bank are a shining example to everyone. They show us that making money is not the most important goal, even for a bank!
